Please remember this video is just for fun, it isn't a be all end all. Some of you are getting pretty hostile in the comments. Everyone's list is going to be different. The reason I had them do a 1v1 against bosses was to show how much damage they do on their own. It would be very difficult for me to measure how good a spirit is if I'm attacking them simultaneously. If a spirt summon can almost kill or completely kill a boss on their own, then obviously they are a strong spirit summon. I also couldn't include EVERY spirit because this would have been like 2 hours long.   Depending on your play style, weapons, and stats, everyone's experience is going to be different.

This is an excellent list - and it‚Äôs why I made sure to get the Dumg Eater puppet‚Ä¶ and man, he is a BEAST! üòÜüòÜ Also, I don‚Äôt think all hawks are the same. Don‚Äôt sleep on ‚ÄúStormhawk Deenh.‚Äù I upgraded it to +9 and it is phenomenal at agro-ing bosses and actually doing quite a bit of constant ticking damage, which prevents their poise meter from regenerating. It also buffs your damage by 20% for 60 seconds every time it lets out a war cry. I used it on the full grown falling star beast and beat it on my first attempt.
Personally, I summon an effective and longer-lasting spirit in some fights, mainly to distract the boss from me from time to time so I can use these opportunities to strike effectively myself. A spirit isn't meant to do my job, but to support me. Sometimes a single spirit is good for that, sometimes a group of spirits is more effective.  I've grown very fond of the three Lone Wolf you get right at the beginning of the game, and they have accompanied and supported me for a long time as I leveled up.  A highly leveled Rotten Stray Dog is also very effective because it's very viable and infects enemies with scarlet rot, which continues to affect them even if the dog dies. An amazing early-game ash as sources of scarlet rot are relatively scarce and most early-game bosses don't have the health to withstand it. The dog itself is very agile and hard to hit.  The "Mimic Tear" shouldn't be missjudged, as it's always just a current copy of the player and can therefore only be as good or as bad as the player themselves at the exact time of summoning.  I've personally had the best experiences with the Black Knife Tich√© so far; it's very durable, very fast and agile, and it also has very good damage output, and, yes, she can kill some bosses all by herself.  Honestly, no joke, but give the Jarwight Puppet a try especially in the earlier phase of the game; you can get it from Seluvis and his quest. It uses a wide variety of pots, from Freezing Pots and Poison Pots/Fetid Pots, to Oil Pots and Swarm Pots, as well as Fire Pots/Redmane Fire Pots and Lightning Pots/Ancient Dragonbolt Pots. Not very strong since the pots thrown are largely random, but nonetheless somewhat entertaining and effective depending of the boss. In any case, it's also good for distracting the boss and to weaken the boss` health, and that's the job of every spirit.

This was a pretty bad video. What you should've done is get agro of the boss without attacking and timed what the spirits do over a certain amount of time. So say 1 summon does 1/4 health in a minute and one does 1/8 health in a minute. Instead you used the summons for what they aren't supposed to be used for and instead of judging them on their damage or skills you're purely judging them on their tanking ability and dodging ability.
The Greatshield Soldiers get so high rated because of a very specific niche use. They are INCREDIBLY effective at fighting Malenia, as long as the player is aggressive. With them, if you also attack fast enough, Malenia will pretty much get sent immediately to phase 2 without even fighting back.  But it's VERY specific and Niche, that's basically the ONLY fight where they are one of the best picks.  But even in that fight they are a huge double edged sword, because if you can't use them to successful stun lock her to death, she basically heals to max HP instantly because she has so many targets lol.

Fun fact about Redmane Knight Ogha, if you use the ash of war "war cry" near him, he roars as well, increasing his attack damage by 20% and he does a rain of gravity arrows similar to Radan's, but only once per summon. You can keep using war cry to temporarily increase his attack, just he cannot reuse his arrow rain ability per summon. Unlike most summons, Redmane Knight Ogha patrols the area of being summoned if all enemies in his line of sight are vanquished. This can be very useful to maintain offense against enemies even if you are far away, unlike summons like Lhutel the headless who follows you instead of attacking if you move farther away. However, the downside is that he cannot escort you through areas or fight bosses such as the tibet river guy since he teleports away out of eyesight.

Hate to say you're wrong, but the nightmaiden and swordstress are S tier for sure. They work incredibly well in most scenarios with multiple builds with their versatility and survivability. Good damage, combos, tank damage do to avoiding and the fact there are two of them trading the agro. Also they cast nightmaiden mist, which is an INCREDIBLE  spell. For context on why this is good: It is essentially an AoE constant damage, and when you use it only one cloud of mist can be out at a time. When you attempt to cast it again the other cloud disapears to where only one can be out at a time...UNLESS you use this spirit ash! Big/slow enemies get eaten alive, and since it doesn't friendly fire on your spirits, it's free damage. You can literally let them do melee and sit back and cast all you want. To finish, I have to say that (even though it is incredible for every build) this is probably the best ash for mages. So much damage, incredibly safe from agro, nightmaiden mist stacking, etc. OP fr.

Great content, but unfortunately kind of a generalized assessment of the summons. There are too many variables to take into account when grading the usefulness of each spirit, and as such it is too hard to judge each of them based off of their performances when fighting a boss. Variations in health pools, poise, attack patterns, fp cost, and different damage types will make each stand out or fail in very different ways depending on the numerous circumstances given to the player. Weeks of our lives would go up in smoke if we ever endeavored to try and figure out all those details. That's not even taking into account the summons relationship with how well it pairs with the player's play style and current build. Don't get me wrong, brother, you're doing God's work here, I love your approach to wanting each of them graded. It's just imagining how each summon would pair crazy well with a bleed build, or a sleep build, or a tank build and I'm constantly keeping aggro, or a glass canon build with a couple "beefy" lizard summons mopping up my left overs, hehe. Basically what I'm saying is that I would love to see how certain builds can exploit or make advantageous the different strengths or weaknesses with each summon. Side note, too, attainment of each summons probably should play a more significant part in the grading system, even though u did kinda account for it. However, with so many people trudging through ng+ and beyond I understand it doesn't really matter that much at that point. Thanks for the content, brother. Can't wait to see more

You list seems to be based on dps alone. You mention how playstyle effects how some of these work then seem to forget it. For instance. I play a strength/faith, low armor zerker style. I like getting in and personal on all bosses and dodge like bat man and drop fully charged strong attacks (light and semi charged attacks too but the fully charge heavy attacks are cherry). This means a ton of these melee summons will get me killed as grabbing the bosses attention at the wrong time and having a wide attack clip me because he made the boss turn is a no-no. Archers are my jam as they barely effect the bosses swiveling around. Jellyfish is legend because it has archer like range, good agro, poison, and it's tanky af. For my style this means she doesn't mess with the bosses positioning, adds poison when she can, and when I need a breather I can deaggro to rebuff/heal/whatever and don't need to worry she will die before I can grab bosses attention again. I think you have a problem keeping bosses stable for ranged summons. When you use ranged summons you want to be playing a very stable in-your-face style. Either an aggressive infighter like myself or a heavy tank shield user.
One of the good things about Banished Knight Engvall is how early in the game you can get him, without making a bee line to some far flug part of the map. He's a little expensive for early game but if you're playing a sorcery focused build he'll basically tank everything for you while you blast from range. Both the banished knights are decent at aoe too with their wide sweeping attacks that'll stagger smaller enemies.

I think these kinds of lists are much more subjective than not simply because of the wide variety of builds you can make. If the game had just one or two builds, then yes, a list would be very much more "This IS the best ___", but for example a mage build character? the Greatshields ashes are FAR better than this list would have you believe, because since aggro works off the last hit or nearest, and there being 5 of them, theyre going to hold that aggro for a long time, and can tank a surprising amount of damage. Whereas Mimic wouldnt be as useful on a mage build, because it doesnt consistently use the best spell in a fight, and isnt good at holding aggro. Meanwhile the Mimic would be fantastic on a bleed build, since thats double the amount of leed sources and output letting it stack very quickly.  The ashes you use very much depend on your build. They can all be subjectively good or bad on their own merits, but ultimately one doesnt work as well as the other in differing circumstances.

IMO you didn't do the jellyfish showcase justice, the point of the jellyfish is that it's a single target that is pretty tanky that constantly shoots ranged attacks at the enemy, drawing aggro away from you for a split second so you can go ham on the boss, and if the boss manages to get to the jellyfish it's likely to survive for a while so you can get control of the boss again, it's meant to survive through the entire boss encounter fairly easily constantly helping you distract the boss, on top of that it applies both poison buildup that can do thousands of damage over the course of a fight and it also apparently applies a damage debuff to enemies it hits. It trivialized both my first encounter with Margit as well as Godrick. It's not gonna do you much good lategame but I think any spirit ash should be rated not only on its lategame potential but also its potential from when it's found. If you go by late game it's better than the wolves, so high C tier I guess, but early game they're both equal and I would rate them fairly high, the wolves even soloed at least two early game bosses for me.  Edit: Also a lot of ashes are pretty niche, for example testing the wolves against a fairly high AoE boss is gonna make the wolves look useless, but if you use them against bosses with a small hit area they can easily solo them.

I see a huge flaw in your testing, and it explains why Jellyfish did so poorly. You sat back and watched the Spirits solo the boss.  Jellyfish is not good for soloing bosses. Jellyfish is good at long range poison assist while having a body that doesn't die easily. The problem with most spirits are that they stand in aoe effects and get melted. Jellyfish doesn't do that, because it floats.   Jellyfish excels when you are initiating and stacking poisons on the boss, because he speeds up your poison while not dying. If you are not attacking the boss, of course Jellyfish didn't work out. The problem is not the Jellyfish. The problem is that you don't use Jellyfish properly. I guarantee that if you attacked the boss immediately after summoning Jellyfish and started stacking poisons, your opinion would change.  Do I think Jellyfish is A tier? Definitely not. Maybe B tier at best, because it's extremely situational and doesn't provide much damage on its own. But Jellyfish is definitely not D tier.  Calling Jellyfish D tier because it doesn't deal as much solo damage as other spirits is the equivalent of saying that swords are D tier weapons because they don't deal as much fire damage as a fire pot.

I feel like there possibly could have been two tier lists for summons, because the way I see it there's two ways to use a summon: 1) Help with DPS, so using the summon for extra damage (ex. Banished Knights Oleg and Engvall, or Black Knife Tiche) 2) Tank/Get Aggro, so using the summon to either tank lots of damage (ex. Dragon Knight Kristoff and Cleanrot Knight Finlay have massive amounts of health, although they both don't attack as much as others), or getting the boss's attention a bunch (ex. Lhutel the Headless has a mix of ranged/melee attacks so she often gets the boss's attention, as bosses often prioritize ranged/spell casters  Maybe separate tier lists would be too much, but just basing it off of one quality when there are some who excel at tanking but suck with dmg and vice versa doesn't seem to be the best idea that it could be. Still, love the effort you put in to your videos, I think you did a wonderful job and overall I think you still did rate pretty much all of the ashes really well.

Interesting note about the land squirts. I discovered that they often spawn in "cheese" areas. Usually a spot where the boss will get stuck or is vulnerable. The dragon knight outside leyndell gets stuck in that area and doesnt move much. The godskin in windmill village can be cheesed through their area in a ring around the windmill. Several bosses have similar situations with them. Its the reason they seem to spawn at a far corner a lot, especially with bosses that are very mobile.

How well a spirit solos a boss seems to be a pretty iffy way to rank them. I understand it's really tough to be scientific about this, but there are a lot of factors here. A lot of spirits just aren't MEANT to solo the boss, they're meant to support you.  Case and point, jellyfish. If you summon it then watch it die to the boss, then you aren't getting good value out of them. They're REALLY inexpensive, they're available almost the entire game, (both of these make them more worthy of upgrading than spirits you can barely afford or barely have any time to use before NG+) and because you aren't using them to solo bosses, they live longer than your test suggests because you're fighting with them. Jellyfish are support DPS, similar to several of the other spirits that I suspect you're underrating.

Imo, the best spirit summon is definitely skeleton militia. Here are my reasons.  Summons like Tiche or Mimic imo do way too much for just a summon. Sometimes, these good summons just literally take you out of the game, which is not really what I am looking for when I am summoning. I hate summons that do "too much" damage. I hate summons that kill bosses for me. I want summons to last long and occasionally distract bosses, but ultimately, I want to defeat bosses myself because overcoming challenge is part of the fun. And in that sense, Skeleton Militia is the best. They do such little damage to bosses that you never feel like you are hand held to victory. However, among all the "bad summons", they are the tankiest because they have a chance to resurrect themselves. So in that sense, they are summons that distract bosses throughout the entire fight but don't directly contribute to the fight in terms of dealing damage. Which is why they are perfect.

Some spirits have different roles compared to others. Some are archers, others are great at dodging, and then you have the tanks. That's what the jellyfish is for. She can survive a long time, but her attack is little more than a taunt to encourage the enemies to attack her. So she *is* useful, but she sucks if you're not helping her. That said, you do eventually get tankier tanks that also damage the enemy, and in the case of those with greater numbers, confuse the boss' ai more effectively. The greatshield soldiers are an example of this. So I do think your assessment of the jellyfish is a bit unfair, it's not fully unwarranted either.

I agree with your tier list for the most part, I would add that there is a number of spirit ashes that you are missing, if you decide you want to do another tier list. One that is a pain to get, but personally i would say is up in the top tier near A or S would be Nepheli Loux Puppet. To get her, you have to do the same thing as you would the dung eater, but when you get the potion from Selivus, you have to make sure you give it to Nepheli after she is in her 'weakened state' (when she is at the bottom of the stairs saying she is a failure to her father in the roundtable area). If you do give her the potion, then you follow the Ranni quest line until selivus is dead and go down to the puppet guy where you can claim the dung eater spirit ash, or the Dolores spirit ash. I would lastly like to mention the Finger Maiden Therolina Puppet. She is another one that you can get that is pretty useful, especially if you're a more tanky build. You can get a chance to see more or less what she does when you fight Radhan, if you summon her. More or less she plays a role of a healer, while still doing bits of damage here and there. Personally, I'd probably rank her around a B, but seeing you test her out would be interesting. Thanks for this great video! I haven't had the time to go through.   Last thing i would say is, thus far, I have found there to be about 68 Spirit ashes. A lot of them are 'ok' early, but late game aren't very useful.

This is just kind of a weird way to compare spirits. Sure, some do lots of damage, but on a normal boss fight even the best spirit ever will be like 1/10 of the total damage done to the boss. So the utility of the spirit is FAR more valuable than their damage. For example, melee spirits ability to do poise damage is much more useful than their actual damage. Ranged spirits are useful because they offer another target, giving you time to heal and counter freely. Damage barely matters on either of those. Jellyfish is good because of its utility, which is arguably more impactful than the most damaging spirit. Like for Melania I would take jellyfish over pretty much any melee spirit, because I really don't want another thing getting hit in melee range healing her.

The basic gist of each tier is:  D tier - Only useful in early game  C tier - Useful up to mid game but die too fast.  B tier - Useful most of the game but have issues like low hp, attacks usually miss, or they don‚Äôt track the enemy unless they‚Äôre close to them.  A tier - All around solid picks that can be optimized based off whatever your characters build is.  S tier - Have the potential to solo late game bosses (can definitely solo mid and early game bosses)

The title of this video doesn't accurately represent what is being tested here. Some summons are built around distracting and tanking rather than DPS output, and inherently perform worse in this test since their intended role is completely disregarded.  The Jellyfish isn't great, but it is by no means the worst summon in the game. It is tanky for the early game and builds poison at distance with ranged attacks while the boss is focused on you. It's not meant for 1v1 scenarios  (which is not really the intention for bell summons in general). The poison build-up can do thousands of HP worth of damage, but you need to distract the boss long enough for him to get the build-up.   He's actually one of the better early game summons vs bosses with huge HP pools like Godrick.   Since you usually have low-level summons early on, some summons like the spirit wolves die within a few seconds to large, wide-sweeping attacks to the likes of Godrick. Jellyfish (even without upgrades) can tank a few hits and survive, more than enough time to let you heal and draw the aggro of the boss afterwards.  A more apt title for this tier list would be "Best summons for soloing bosses".

JellyFish is not an ash to take on a boss on its own like the Mimic, Black knife Tiche, etc. Jelly Fish is suppose to be use as a distraction for the enemy,  a break for you to heal, power up, do charge attacks, etc. In this scenarios the JellyFish is actually on of the best Ashes because 1 it is tankie so it will not be 1 shot by some enemies, 2 it has a range attack so if you are fighting in a corner and the Jellyfish attacks many enemies will start slow walking towards it and last but not least 3 it does poison damage which is great if you also have poison build up weapon/skills. Bonus about Latenna: I also thought she was stationnary and pretty good already... but then I found out today through a youtube clip she has a mobility option: wolves. If you summon her in a zone containing wild wolves, and one of them gets close to her, she will tame it and ride it, increasing her attacking speed and allowing her to run around at mach speed. It doesn't really do anything in most, if not all, boss fights, since wolves are mostly found in the overworld and not in boss rooms, but it's a cool hidden mechanic unique to her.  Edit: Many of the comments have specified this to me, so I will correct a bit of misinformation on my part: it doesn't work on ALL wolves, only SOME wolves. They have to be about as big as the wolf she had when you get her ashes, so dire wolf size. The wolves in front of the Ranni Castle work, but I don't know if they appear in other places in the world.

This is a great video.  It displays all these ashes in action even though I kinda disagree with how the tests are performed.  You‚Äôre not wrong at all about the lower tier ashes being fragile or not dealing enough damage, but this testing environment favors the hardiest and brutalist among the summons.  The lower tier ones function better as extensions of your toolkit.  The wolves work great on foes that stagger easily as there‚Äôs three of them and they‚Äôre relentless, but work together best with a player who is just as relentless, gaining more aggro to keep you both alive and pummeling the boss so they can‚Äôt fight back.  Similarly Dolores and Miss Jellyfish work best when YOU focus on drawing most of the aggro, as they‚Äôll take some away while shooting at the boss to give you a chance to breathe but you have to take it back to make sure they don‚Äôt get overwhelmed (and obvi best used on foes you know are more vulnerable to sleep/poison respectively).  Of course the hardy more expensive ones are more versatile in just being a staunch ally to fight alongside you, but the cheaper spirits function well if you‚Äôre using them as tools for their intended purpose. I'm sure someone already said it somewhere in the 1000+ comments, but something important to remember about some of the summons is that they aren't meant to solo the boss.  I completely agree that a summon that melts the boss alone is S+ tier, but some of the ones ranked low are still amazing.  Jellyfish is great at distracting the boss, and if it can be poisoned even better.  Still better if it's a boss in a terrible arena with floor damage, or a boss that puts crap on the floor. Rotten Stray is amazing because of Scarlet Rot.  Get that on a boss, and just run around staying alive.  Poof.  Boss down. Running a high crit build?  Lone Wolves are great at staggering bosses.  Because there are 3, and they are so aggressive they break through poise fast opening up bosses to crits.  All that being said, I did appreciate this list showing which ashes are just monsters.  My first playthrough is focused on just doing as much as I can, and isn't capitalizing on any specific build so having a monster summon is helpful.  All-in-all, enjoyed the video, and the list.
So what‚Äôs the best one?
If you're measuring the summons without doing anything at all then that's going to skew your results.  Not all the ashes are meant to solo bosses. Jellyfish in particular needs time to apply the poison, she's not great, but she's not garbage either as this video suggests. Finlay is situationally good depending on resistances, but she's situational.  Lhutel is easily S tier, she has NO situation where she gets annihilated and she's one of the tankiest summons for working WITH players the aforementioned issue with trying to summon them alone skewing results shows heavily with Lhutel and the fact that she got A tier in this video when that's not even her job should show how good she actually is when you're not simply trying to watch your game. Video also didn't bother to mention that Lhutel does indeed have ranged attacks as well, but due to how they ran the experiment you don't see Lhutel use them if she has aggro, but her ranged attacks help her pull aggro if you take it away from her once again if you're not simply watching her fight and doing literally nothing like in the video.  Dung Eater is worse than Lhutel if you want a tank and he's not as offensive as Tiche. Nephali Loux performs about equivalently and costs significantly less FP (24) if you give her the potion. Dung Eater's damage is largely dependent on Bleed as well, whilst he keeps his tankiness so he's not entirely situational like Finlay, he does have several bosses he doesn't work nearly as well against that even the tankier Lhutel can outperform him damage wise.  Missing one of the best non-special summons in the Godrick Soldier Ashes, but this type of experiment would skew them as poor. Cheap and tanky if you're desperate for a low cost summon. Great Shield Soldiers are tankier but also more expensive, by a decent margin if you don't invest in mind at all you can still summon Godrick Soldier Ashes but you won't be able to summon Great Shield Ashes. Giant Rats should get a special mention for being absolutely free of any cost all together and being surprisingly not garbage.  In Closing:  Lhutel for tank, Tiche for damage, Mimic tear can easily beat them both in both category if spec'd to work with the Mimic Tear's new drawbacks (high defense resist, high poise, and a strong weapon for basic attacks works best with the Mimic post nerf since it uses the Weapon Art significantly less that doesn't matter nearly as much anymore) Dung Eater is good for status support. His shout decreases the enemies defense and resistances to ALL status effects, whislt he only builds bleed you can use Dung Eater to build poison, rot, bleed or frost thinking of him as a tanky support Ash with good AI. Keep Latenna in S because if you don't mind holding aggro she's just as strong DPS-wise as Tiche and signficantly cheaper that somebody without a lot of Mind investment can even use and that's your S tier. Redmane Knight Ogha does NOT follow you after being summoned unlike most ashes and patrols the area in a very small range, in larger boss arenas this can even keep him from engaging the boss if you summon him too far away like at the start of entering the field. He's unreliable. His bow is also magical so if the enemy resists magic damage heavily he struggles as he heavily prefers ranged combat to melee combat if he has the choice which if the player pulls aggro he will primarily only use his bow which can be unreliable accuracy-wise when trying to hit moving targets which in turn keeps him from drawing aggro from the player and making him more or less a worse damage Ash than Tiche or Latenna in those scenarios. Since you get limited Ghost Gloveworts to get +10 spirits it's smarter to choose special spirits that are ALWAYS reliable and Redmane Knight Ogha isn't one of those.  Quick tier of standout Ashes and some mentioned in the video simply because they were in the video. Also note there is a trick with the flask of wonderous physick that can render FP cost moot, you just need the Cerulean Hidden Tear and you get 15 seconds where you have no FP cost including for summoning Ashes so if you have that cost is no longer a factor at all and you can pick from S tier with impunity, it also drops Latenna down because she's more of a extremely good for the FP cost Ash than actually being fully better than Tiche as they have similar DPS values and Tiche has more going for her what with being able to move and all. S+ Mimic Tear (still good enough to be in a class of it's own went built properly for it) S Lhutel, Tiche, Latenna, Dung Eater  A Nephali Loux (Dung Eater outperforms Nephali when everything goes his way, they're about even when it doesn't, but Nephali is cheaper) Azula Beastmen, Greatshield Soldier, Ancestral Follower (no reason to use him over Latenna really though) B Redmane Ogha (inconsistent and significantly weaker if the player is participating), Kaiden Sellsword (tanky single character Ash, better than Greatshield Soldier Ash when the boss has large AoEs other than that usually worse and costs more to deploy), Giant Rat Ash (completely free of any cost actually decent at dealing damage, frail and vulnerable to AoE very similar to Lone Wolf Ashes, but without the cost, best Ash for 0 Mind build outside of Mimic Tear honestly) C Godrick Soldier Ash (extremely cheap relative and tanky), Rotten Stray (stronger poison than Jellyfish only good when poison is good, but really cheap which helps the ranking), Radahn Soldier Ash (About as tanky as Godrick Ashes, but stronger however at a higher cost to use as well), Lone Wolf Ashes (cheap damage dealing ash with decent poise damage, but frail and vulnerable to AoEs) D Jellyfish (treat the Jellyfish like Latenna, it doesn't move very quickly and to shine needs the player to draw aggro, has a high HP pool, but it can get hit a lot if the boss has quick successive attacks and only even remotely usable if the boss can be poisoned)

This is a great video.  It displays all these ashes in action even though I kinda disagree with how the tests are performed.  You‚Äôre not wrong at all about the lower tier ashes being fragile or not dealing enough damage, but this testing environment favors the hardiest and brutalist among the summons.  The lower tier ones function better as extensions of your toolkit.  The wolves work great on foes that stagger easily as there‚Äôs three of them and they‚Äôre relentless, but work together best with a player who is just as relentless, gaining more aggro to keep you both alive and pummeling the boss so they can‚Äôt fight back.  Similarly Dolores and Miss Jellyfish work best when YOU focus on drawing most of the aggro, as they‚Äôll take some away while shooting at the boss to give you a chance to breathe but you have to take it back to make sure they don‚Äôt get overwhelmed (and obvi best used on foes you know are more vulnerable to sleep/poison respectively).  Of course the hardy more expensive ones are more versatile in just being a staunch ally to fight alongside you, but the cheaper spirits function well if you‚Äôre using them as tools for their intended purpose. Granted he isn't as tanky as some other summons like crystalians, but with dual greatswords he staggers bosses a lot in fights, good for fights that you need an aggressive partner to fight like Dual Gargoyles or Dragon Soldier. I would say they also fall off late game, but can at least be summoned in places like Volcano Manor or Lake of Rot and wont die to environmental damage.

Early to mid game my favorite is the Godrick Soldiers.  At only +3 or 4, they've carried on through full boss battles, allowing me to unlock the more legendary summons to replace them.  IMHO these guys are the best early all rounders, especially since you can get them at the same time as the Wolves and Jellyfish.  As a new character, going against Margit/Godrick, if I had to choose between the Wolves, Jellyfish or them... Its the Godrick Soldiers every time.  Both have hammers and brass shields, with one also having a crossbow.  If the boss is close to them, they go at them with good damage and tank hits with their brass shields/decent health pools.  If the boss agros on to you, the hammer one will pursue aggressively, while the crossbow will begin peppering it with bolts.  I rarely have to circle and dodge for more than a few seconds before they grab agro back.
Marionette Soldiers are an easy A tier at LEAST.  They pull aggro incredibly easily because of how often they attack. This is perfect for every build, allowing them to set up and deal maximum damage with relatively no fear of the boss attacking them. Not only this, but the two of them deal HELLA stance damage and can easily knock multiple bosses in the game by themselves. The only downside is that if they deal too much damage, they could knock the boss out of the staggered state.  Oh! And these two boys are actually quite tanky, so they can hold aggro for awhile!

Ok.  So.   What the actual fuck is the point of only testing spirit summons solo vs bosses?   Sure, it's one useful metric but, practically speaking, when do you ever use spirit summons for that?  The point of spirit summons is to manage your opponents aggro, and or their posture, along with to add dps.   For instance, The point of the jellyfish, is to be a tank and to mess with boss ai. Yes, it sucks ass for damage but that should be the last reason you summon the jellifish.   Other examples, like the wolves and demi humans, can add a lot of additional poise damage. They also help split up aggro.  At the very least you should have made a few categories.   Sometimes you want a bunch of mobs, sometimes you just want one. Sometimes you need a ranged attack and sometimes you need a specific damage type. Other times you're trying to stack status effects and or damage types, while other times you need them to resist certain status effects and damage types.    I would argue that's best to have one summon to help double down on your strengths, a 2nd summon for balanced encounters and a 3rd to help shore up your weaknesses. I would say that there are different tiers of each type of need for different character builds.  Lastly fp cost can be a huge limiting factor and can have a direct impact on which ashes are s tier for various builds.

Take this tier list as a spirit ash 1v1 power tier. In real play-through ashes tiers are really depending on what build you are and what aspect of help do you need.  For tanking the boss when you are a mage: Greatshield soldiers S+ For versatility: Mimic Tear S+ For dealing damage if you are the one with a great shield: Letenna the Albinauric/Black knife Tiche S+ And for your progress in the game, it's not like you can single handily complete Ranni's quest to get Tiche or venture through the sewer for the Dung Eater.

Piece of advice: though your testing wouldn't show it, Oleg is one of the best summons in the game against Malenia. Not only is he tanky enough to survive a full on Waterfowl Dance with a good chunk of health remaining, nearly every single attack he does can stagger her, plus his dash is an excellent gap closer. He's not as high-damaging as Tiche, but he survives longer and distracts her better, and is more reliable at staggering her than Mimic (post-patch, at least).
